{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","title":"Proof That Your Friends Are the Best Dating App Editors","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213168","description":"<p><em>In partnership with <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a>.</em></p>\n<p><em>A portion of proceeds from Man Repeller’s partnership with Inner Circle is dedicated to charitable organizations that support social justice causes and to individual projects by BIPOC creatives.</em></p>\n<hr />\n<p>People say that friends make the best dating app editors for a reason. Sparking intrigue in the hearts of your suitors by way of a dating profile is no easy feat, and there’s nothing quite like a close friend to bounce ideas off of and to function as your system of checks and balances (you’ll repay them with a pint of ice cream, I’m sure).</p>\n<p>Two pairs of friends recently proved this theory correct when they documented the experience of setting up two <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a> dating profiles: one for Naydeline and one for Steffi, both creative types based in New York City. Their friends Leslie and Tess, who are both spoken for, came in with the assist and lent some authority to the project. <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a> is a global app, most popular in England, Brazil, and the Netherlands, for lighthearted people who are serious about dating. Designed to celebrate the nuances of each user, Inner Circle stands apart with its emphasis on facilitating real connection offline, getting you closer to meeting your match in person rather than sinking a lot of time into chatting on-app.</p>\n<p>Here, each friend-pair annotated the profiles they made with the behind-the-scenes, sausage-making conversations and thought processes that go into setting up a dating profile that rings true both on- and offline.</p>\n<hr />\n<h2>Steffi, a site curator in New York, looking for a romantic prospect who can appreciate a pajama shirt worn outdoors</h2>\n<p><em>Steffi and Tess teamed up to take on Steffi’s <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a> profile. While it doesn’t quite translate on paper, much of this conversation was conducted in British accents. Here are the rules of the road, according to Tess and Steffi.</em></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213203 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Steffi_V2-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2100\" height=\"2345\" /></p>\n<p><strong>1. Always pick an even number of photos, for reasons based on gut feeling alone.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Let&#8217;s do photos. I&#8217;m feeling very visual.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> So the first one I have is on my Instagram. Me at the beach. You know the vibes. I think it&#8217;s nice, right? It&#8217;s like, not too scandy and then it&#8217;s still got my face—</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> You&#8217;re a highlight in this. You&#8217;ve got your angle on lock, my friend.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Oh, thank you. I appreciate it. It takes practice. It takes dedication.</p>\n<p><strong><img class=\" wp-image-213189 alignleft\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Steffi_2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"505\" height=\"505\" /><br />\nTess:</strong> Oftentimes too, this photo of you from your week in L.A., the cheetah-print shirt, it gives me intrigue. I like it. I mean not as much as your first one, because your first one should be clear.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Yeah, that was a little blurry. I feel like that one is kind of edgy, cool girl. And then it&#8217;s like, &#8220;Oh, pajamas as outside clothes. Very innovative.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Right, it also weeds out the normies right away.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> It weeds out the British version of men with fish.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> How many photos do you think is not too many, not too few, but just enough?</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> I usually think four or five, right?</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I personally don&#8217;t like five. I like even numbers. Also, what are your thoughts on&#8230; do you want to be one of the people who puts a meme as your last one?</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> I feel like that&#8217;s not a thing anymore.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong>: For the fourth photo, I think I&#8217;m going to put one of me and you, because it&#8217;s just one with yourself.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I like putting a photo of you with somebody else to prove that you are not a bot as the third or fourth photo. I was thinking about that for the first photo, but I can&#8217;t stand the “me or her?” dating profile. Anyway, you look so cute. And I look like an eel. It doesn&#8217;t matter what I look like. It&#8217;s fine. That&#8217;s a great picture of you.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> So iconic. That was a good photo. You also look really cute in that—you&#8217;re just like a happy, happy jelly baby.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I do look happy jelly in that photo. I&#8217;m fine with it.</p>\n<p><strong>2. Create intrigue with a mysterious job title.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Do you want to put your occupation?</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> I just wrote “writer.” I didn&#8217;t put anything else. Because I feel like people won&#8217;t understand what a “site curator” is.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Hear me out, like that could be potentially—</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Interesting?</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> &#8220;What&#8217;s a site curator? I would love to learn more about what you curate on your site.&#8221; I mean, I don&#8217;t know, probably not but&#8230;</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Is that more intriguing than being a writer?</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I actually don&#8217;t know.</p>\n<p><strong>3. Pick a favorite place outdoors.</strong></p>\n<p><strong><img class=\" wp-image-213188 alignright\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Steffi_1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"302\" height=\"302\" /><br />\nTess:</strong> For your favorite place&#8230;</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Let&#8217;s do Prospect Park.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I think that&#8217;s cute. It&#8217;s also kind of an invite. Because in a pandemic, that&#8217;s still viable.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Actually, that&#8217;s real. Very good point.</p>\n<p><strong>4. Be honest about how you spend your free time.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> How do I spend my free time?</p>\n<p><strong>Tess: </strong>Basically it says, &#8220;Share what makes you interesting.&#8221; You&#8217;re like, &#8220;I have a middle part, love. And it looks good actually.”</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> &#8220;I have a natural middle part, and what about it?&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Oh my God. Imagine having a natural part. That&#8217;s a dream. How do you spend your time? Oh my God. Tell them about your 40 jokes a day.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Oh my God.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess: </strong>&#8220;I am writing 40 jokes a day for a year, FYI.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi: </strong>Yep. Actually, maybe I should write that. I feel like all my things I do in my free time are just writing different things.</p>\n<p><strong>5. Prompt a conversation with a conversation prompt.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Do you want to do an open question? Maybe like, &#8220;Do you do the cooking? Do you do the cleaning?&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi: </strong>&#8220;What&#8217;s your dish-washing process? Describe your dish-washing process.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Tess: </strong>Hang on. That&#8217;s not bad, because it&#8217;s kind of necessary. You don&#8217;t want a guy who just&#8230; I&#8217;m having this vision of a grown man filling up the sink with water and just dumping plates aggressively and throwing them on the rack—</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> I think the process of washing dishes is a fragile one because what I do is, I put the plug into the sink and then I put the soap in and then I turn the water on, so that the water gets evenly nice and bubbly across. And I feel like that&#8217;s not—</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> You fill up the sink? That is not common, no.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi: </strong>Yeah, because I don&#8217;t turn on the sink again. I just use that water. And then I wash all my dishes in that water, which I feel like is not common practice.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> This could be a great way to find a man near Prospect Park with a dishwasher.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> “Who wants to play mermaids with me?” Wait, that should be the quote.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess: </strong>That&#8217;s a good one.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Okay. I&#8217;m changing it. I&#8217;m changing the profile prompts to: &#8220;Do you want to play mermaids?&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Tess: </strong>And I think that will naturally attract men who do dishes well.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Yes, I do agree.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Kind of a two-for-one?<br />\n<img class=\" wp-image-213190 alignleft\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Steffi_.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"349\" height=\"349\" /></p>\n<p><strong>6. Hear them out: a philosophy behind withholding your favorite spots.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> I think not adding where you would want to go for a drink could be good, too, because I feel like it&#8217;s kind of a miss to meet people who like the same place as you do. Or to depend on them liking the same places as you for your only common-ground trait. It&#8217;s so fun to show people places they&#8217;d never been.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Yeah. That is so much fun. And really, in a place like New York City, there&#8217;s always a place you haven&#8217;t been.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> *wrapping up voice* Yay. That was fun.</p>\n<p><strong>Tess:</strong> Mission possible.</p>\n<p><strong>Steffi:</strong> Mission possible. Oh my God.</p>\n<h2>Naydeline, a journalist in New York, looking for a fellow Francophile</h2>\n<p><em>Naydeline and Leslie worked together on Naydeline’s profile, while Leslie’s apartment was being haunted by an unidentified presence. They discovered that on <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a>, you can find other people who were born on your birthday. Here’s a peek through the keyhole at how Leslie and Naydeline arranged Naydeline’s profile just so.</em></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213191 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Naydeline.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"2100\" height=\"2345\" /></p>\n<p><strong>1. When it comes to photos, make a charismatic first impression.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> So do you want somebody that you can travel with, or do you want someone to go to museums with you?</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> Both.</p>\n<p><strong><img class=\" wp-image-213192 alignleft\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Naydeline_1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"271\" height=\"271\" />Leslie:</strong> Use the one on the boat that I sent you. You look fun, charismatic, and like you&#8217;re comfortable in your own skin. I&#8217;m a fan of nature.</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> I&#8217;m going to use it, even though I&#8217;m wearing sunglasses.</p>\n<p><strong>2. You contain multitudes: Allow certain categorizations to be open for interpretation.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> I’m saying you’re a runner, because you run from the train to class to your internship to back home.</p>\n<p><strong>3. Leverage your arts and culture preferences toward your preferred brand of dates.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Concertgoer, theater lover, musical fan, art lover. You&#8217;re all of it, bro.</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> If they weren&#8217;t so expensive, I&#8217;d go to Broadway shows every weekend, I feel like. They&#8217;re so cool.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> I&#8217;m going to put “theater lover.” Let&#8217;s see if we can get you a man who takes you to the theater.</p>\n<p><strong>4. To start a conversation, kindly request some memes.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Would you say hi, or hello, or hola? &#8220;Hi everybody, I&#8217;m Naydeline.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> This isn&#8217;t LinkedIn—this is a dating app. You can talk about what I like to do.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> &#8220;I love adventure&#8221;? I don&#8217;t know.</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline: </strong>That&#8217;s so corny. Everyone who says “I&#8217;m adventurous” on their dating profile is not adventurous. I&#8217;m going to tell you that right now. I like to include a little game in my bio, something like, &#8220;Send me your favorite meme, or send me your best pickup line.&#8221; That&#8217;ll help people start a conversation, I guess.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> &#8220;I love memes.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> “I love memes”? Oh my god.</p>\n<p><strong><img class=\" wp-image-213193 alignright\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Naydeline_2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"420\" height=\"420\" />Leslie:</strong> &#8220;Send me a good meme.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> I have: “If I had the time and money, I would travel more.” There are 81 available characters left. Or is this bio enough?</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline: </strong>I feel like it ends weirdly. Maybe put some places I want to travel to: &#8220;Looking for someone to go to blank with.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> You want to go to Paris, I know you&#8217;re bothering me about that again.</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> I do want to go to Paris. I spend way too much time watching Parisian YouTubers.</p>\n<p><strong>5. Strategize for a good first date.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Where would you like to go for a date? Food?</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> Yeah. I love that. Honestly, I feel like dates at restaurants can be awkward, but I feel like you also get to know people better.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Yeah, and you can get a sense of someone&#8217;s manners.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Okay, where would you like to go for a drink? A rooftop bar?</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> To be honest, a rooftop bar. Anything that&#8217;s just not that basic, like I don&#8217;t want to sit in a dark-ass bar. There should be nice views.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Okay, so how about a rooftop bar to get some air and to get to know you?</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong>: Yeah. I like that.</p>\n<p><strong>6. Vocalize that you’re open to new places.</strong></p>\n<p><strong><img class=\" wp-image-213194 alignleft\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Inner-Circle_Profile_Naydeline_3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"424\" height=\"424\" />Naydeline: </strong>I haven’t been to a lot of bars. Unless restaurants with bars count. Can you skip that? I&#8217;ve been to like one bar. Is it called Barcade? I think it is.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Okay, I said, &#8220;My favorite place is a Barcade, but that&#8217;s actually the only bar I&#8217;ve been to. Looking for fun new bars, any recommendations?&#8221; Because that could be a conversation starter.</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> True, okay. Dating profile pro.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Well I&#8217;ve never really done this, I&#8217;ve only done one dating profile. But it was when I was in Greece and I was dared to, because I&#8217;ve been in a long-term, committed relationship</p>\n<p><strong>Naydeline:</strong> I know, so I was surprised you&#8217;re doing so well.</p>\n<p><strong>Leslie:</strong> Hey!</p>\n<p>Ready to get in the mix with <a href=\"https://m.theinnercircle.co/?utm_campaign=mr\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inner Circle</a>? Experts","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213457","description":"<p>When I look into my crystal ball, I see myself sleeping on a mattress on the floor for the next two to three months. Unfortunately, there’s a defect in this crystal ball, so it doesn’t do the legwork of specifying exactly what kind of mattress it is: Is it firm, does it have a little give, is it made of organic latex, is it better for a side-sleeper or a stomach-sleeper? Does it share a name with a friendly ghost, or a secondary color, or a popular fruit often spread on toast? Does comedian Neal Brennan <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/B_vDboCD8bm/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">have the right idea</a>?</p>\n<p>These days, the world of sheets and pillows and mattresses-in-a-box and duvet covers is supersaturated. When my eyes glazed over Krispy-Kreme-style after reading my eleventh mattress-centric message board, I decided to change my approach and beeline to a few well-rested experts for their personal recommendations on how to concoct the perfect bed. Below are a bunch of enthusiastic suggestions that’ll make sleeping in your bed feel like snoozing on a CBD-infused cumulus cloud.</p>\n<hr />\n<h2>Sheets</h2>\n<p><strong>Liz Eichholz, co-founder and creative director of <a href=\"https://weezietowels.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Weezie Towels</a></strong><br />\n<strong>Liz&#8217;s favorite sheets:</strong> “Here ends the never-ending hunt for the perfect set of sheets! I am obsessed with this super-soft set from Ettitude: the <a href=\"https://fave.co/33UaSbm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bamboo Lyocell Sheet Set</a>. I love that they’ve held up well in the wash and don’t wrinkle. Bonus points for keeping this warm sleeper cool throughout the night.”</p>\n<p><strong>Elizabeth Tamkin, market strategist of Man Repeller<br />\n</strong><strong>Elizabeth’s favorite summer sheets: </strong>“This <a href=\"https://fave.co/349DT35\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">100% Linen Sheet set from Linoto</a> is locally made and the set includes the whole shebang: flat sheet, fitted sheet, and two pillow cases. They also come in 25 different colors to suit your style. This is the perfect summer sheet set that remains soft and sturdy wash after wash.”</p>\n<p><strong>Gyan Yankovich, managing editor of Man Repeller</strong><br />\n<strong>Gyan’s favorite linen sheets: </strong>“My boyfriend didn&#8217;t get a good night&#8217;s sleep for the first two years we lived in NYC—in the summer the weather was too hot, and in the winter, our building&#8217;s heat was on full blast. He spent a lot of time researching the best linen sheets and came away with these ones, the <a href=\"https://bit.ly/3kG4Jp6\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Pottery Barn Belgian Linen Sheet set</a>. I was apprehensive to spend so much money on sheets, but we did and they&#8217;ve been a game-changer! 3</div>\n</section>\n\n<h2>Mattresses and bed frames</h2>\n<p><strong>Allison Petty, design director of <a href=\"https://www.hyphenandco.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hyphen &#38; Co.</a></strong><br />\n<strong>Allison’s favorite mattress:</strong> “<a href=\"https://www.avocadogreenmattress.com/?utm_source=google&#38;utm_medium=cpc&#38;utm_campaign=b-mattress&#38;ar_clx=yes&#38;ar_channel=google&#38;ar_campaign=830413436&#38;ar_adgroup=41789894359&#38;ar_ad=386547335662&#38;ar_strategy=search&#38;gclid=EAIaIQobChMIxqOj9rCY6wIVkozICh2h3gT_EAAYASAAEgIk8vD_BwE\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Avocado mattress</a> offers both green and vegan options which is something we really love. The quality and comfort is there, while also committing to a more earth-friendly product.”</p>\n<p><strong>Ellen van Dusen, founder of <a href=\"https://www.dusendusen.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dusen Dusen</a></strong><br />\n<strong>Ellen’s favorite bed frame:</strong> “I have the <a href=\"https://www.dwr.com/bedroom-beds/nest-storage-bed/1727.html?lang=en_US\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">nest storage bed from Design Within Reach</a>, and as a borderline hoarder, it is perfect. I do a lot of &#8216;testing&#8217; for new bedding when we get samples for my line… which means I have way too much bedding… which takes up a lot of space. The bed frame easily lifts and there&#8217;s an empty compartment underneath, which is where I store it all. Also, it just looks really good and has a soft headboard. It&#8217;s relatively low to the ground and has an aesthetic I&#8217;d describe as plump, the visual equivalent of how I want my furniture to feel.”<br />\n<em>[Ed. note: while still a splurge, the <a href=\"https://www.eq3.com/us/en/product/ck9cyugiu000h3b5n5cq6padm/bedroom/beds/upholstered-beds/cello-storage-bed-fabric?ck2xt209a04ii0102nee6atez=ck6codw1v1bnl0114o1v9gdt8&#38;ck6codvyo1bn00114bg82qdsf=ck6codvyu1bn10114gunyxxb9&#38;cjv5o1pn2065s0186zx728ixs=cjv5o1pn6065t0186gq5ybj3i&#38;cjv5o1pn2065s0186zx728ixs%7CPrimaryColour=HA064&#38;cjv5o1pn2065s0186zx728ixs%7CBaseLeg=HU273&#38;cjv5o1pni065u0186zp0o8pht=ck5o3kumg0im40130nosbcbsw&#38;cjv5o1pni065u0186zp0o8pht%7CPrimaryColour=HR241&#38;cjv5o1pns065w0186jvuo7aiw=cjv5o1pnw065x01864tvdni4i&#38;cjv5lq8ww05wf0190gyv0fx44=cjv5lq8x205wg0190frpju1tq&#38;ck6codw241bno01141znea8jp=ck6codw2a1bnp01147ibrnqba&#38;cjv5o91zk066e0186dd6w00dk=cjv5o91zp066f0186gmbp4y2y&#38;cjv5o91zk066e0186dd6w00dk%7CPrimaryColour=HK690&#38;cjv5o91zk066e0186dd6w00dk%7CBaseLeg=HU273&#38;cjv5o91zu066g0186ciosf8c7=cjv5o91zy066h01863fc08w4i&#38;cjv5o91zu066g0186ciosf8c7%7CPrimaryColour=HR241&#38;cjv5o9204066i0186ggqcq1q1=ckcf1x20a00013b5ouxqzs831&#38;cjv5lot1u05ux0186mmr8qb7c=cjv5lot1y05uy0186bd7f3xo4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cello storage bed</a> by EQ3 is an alternative to the Design Within Reach model!]</em></p>\n<p><strong>Tavia Forbes and Monet Masters, principal interior designers of Forbes Masters</strong><br />\n<strong>Tavia and Monet’s headboard tip:</strong> “We often recommend a bold headboard, like <a href=\"https://bit.ly/3kEWfi1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">this tufted one by CB2</a>, to our clients. src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script></p>\n<h2>Pillows</h2>\n<p><strong>Tiffany Wilkinson, creative director of Man Repeller</strong><br />\n<strong>Tiffany’s favorite pregnancy pillow:</strong> “I ordered this <a href=\"https://fave.co/2Y1o6PU\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Parachute Home Body Pillow</a> as an alternative to the <a href=\"https://www.google.com/search?q=pregnancy+pillow&#38;source=lnms&#38;tbm=isch&#38;sa=X&#38;ved=2ahUKEwiNhIWC7ZXrAhU_gnIEHfqHCp8Q_AUoAnoECCAQBA&#38;biw=1418&#38;bih=766\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">crazy shaped pregnancy pillows</a>, hoping that I&#8217;d be able to keep it as part of my bedding set up post-pregnancy. After I ordered it, I had buyer’s remorse, wondering if it was too self-indulgent of a purchase. Once it arrived, it became an instant game-changer—I immediately started sleeping better, my whole body felt so supported, and it&#8217;s great to have something so substantial to spoon. I love the pillow so much I even gave it a name. My partner is a little envious of all the love my body pillow is getting, but if I get out of bed before him, I&#8217;ll look over and see him fast asleep straddling the pillow in a deep blissful spoon.”</p>\n<p><strong>Liz of Weezie’s favorite sham:</strong> “I’m a sucker for layers and an eclectic mix of playful patterns throughout my home—and that extends to our bedroom! I’ve long been drawn to the gorgeous prints from Biscuit Home. Next up for me: this Texan-inspired print that reminds me of my hometown of Austin, the <a href=\"https://www.biscuit-home.com/collections/prints-bedding-collection/products/marfa-standard-sham-1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Biscuit Home Marfa Euro Sham</a>.”</p>\n<p><strong>Allison of Hyphen’s favorite throw pillows:</strong> “<a href=\"https://milayaproject.org/collections/throw-pillows\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Milaya Project</a> has great embroidered throw pillows that have a ton of personality. We love that they also help support the art of South Sudanese refugees.”</p>\n<p><strong>Ellie Buckingham and Miri Buckland, co-founders of <a href=\"http://www.thelandinghome.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The Landing</a></strong><br />\n<strong>Ellie and Miri’s favorite throw pillow:</strong> &#8220;We love the <a href=\"https://www.k-apostrophe.com/throw-pillows/big-rock-throw-pillow\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Big Rock Throw Pillow</a> from one of our new partners, K-Apostrophe. K&#8217;era takes neutral, soothing colors but applies them in interesting ways that make these pillows a great statement piece for many colors of bedding without being too over the top.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Yours truly<br />\nEdith’s favorite slender pillow:</strong> “If you, like me, sometimes only want a nominal lift from the mattress for your noggin, the Vermont Country Store makes <a href=\"https://www.vermontcountrystore.com/slender-standard-bed-pillow/product/43240\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">just the slender pillow</a> for you. I’d dress her up with <a href=\"https://www.goodeeworld.com/collections/pillows-mats/products/pillow-sham-anholt-stripes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">this brown striped Tekla sham sold by Goodee</a>.”</p>\n<p><strong>Elizabeth’s favorite decorative “body” pillow:</strong>  “I suppose this isn’t technically a body pillow but during the night I like a pillow to hug and this <a href=\"https://www.jungalow.com/collections/justina-blakeney-pillows/products/chloe-hook-pillow-by-justina-blakeney\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hook Pillow by Justina Blakeney</a> is a great substitute for when my dog doesn’t want to sleep beside me. It also happens to be absolutely beautiful (I love many of Justina Blakeney’s designs and find that their price points are great)—a nice touch to a made bed when you’re not sleeping.”</p>\n<p><strong>Megan Hopp, <a href=\"https://www.meganhopp.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">interior designer</a></strong><br />\n<strong>Megan’s favorite lumbar pillow:</strong> “Every bed should have a lumbar pillow, and <a href=\"https://fave.co/3gURkHn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">St. Frank</a> has my favorite selection. While I love color and pattern, I still opt for a calmer combination in the bedroom and <a href=\"https://fave.co/3gURkHn\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">these pillows</a> are perfectly patterned. 18:18:24","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","title":"Are Sweatpants Really Forever?","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213446","description":"<p>“<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2020/08/06/magazine/fashion-sweatpants.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sweatpants Forever</a>”—the recent <em>New York Times Magazine</em> headline proved that a drawstring has tremendous potential to scandalize. On August 6th, the magazine’s cover story detailed the unraveling of the fashion industry, accelerated by the COVID-19 pandemic. The narrative centers around Scott Sternberg, founder of Band of Outsiders and Entireworld, and the trials and tribulations of <a href=\"https://fave.co/2MelZBy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">his direct-to-consumer and ultra-popular sweatsuit</a> (you know the one).</p>\n<p>In the story, writer Irina Aleksander laid bare how the fashion industry perpetuated its own brokenness, walking the reader through how exactly the wheels fell off. The revelation of how industry stakeholders are teetering on the edge of their own margins rings familiar: the parallels to <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/04/23/magazine/closing-prune-restaurant-covid.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gabrielle Hamilton’s well-circulated April 2020 <em>NYT Magazine</em> story</a> about the future of her restaurant Prune, and of New York’s restaurant industry at large, are manifold. In both cases, the pandemic has necessitated an internal reckoning. Aleksander’s story prompts questions of how these brands, and their backers, can shed the bad practices they’ve long relied on, and forge a new and better path ahead. A dissection of a system mid-crumble is bound to leave the reader in search of solutions—at least that’s how I felt while reading it.</p>\n<p>The onus is on everyone—the producer, the customer, and the seller—to create, consume and distribute more thoughtfully. I’ve been thinking about the utopian fashion brand as one that sits at the center of this Venn diagram: it’s environmentally sustainable, the range of sizes it offers is reflective of the population, it delivers a quality product destined for longevity in the buyer’s closet, at an affordable price point that stills allows for the company to be profitable and for the company’s employees—from the factory to the corporate headquarters—to be treated ethically and compensated fairly. It sounds like a pipe dream—is it actually?</p>\n<p>I’ve found glimpses of optimism bubbling on a smaller scale. I had ordered an OOKIOH swimsuit sight unseen in the mail and, happy with the fit and quality of the underwired <a href=\"https://fave.co/3fPiCh4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Como top</a> and the high-waisted <a href=\"https://fave.co/31yuDm0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dominican bottom</a>, had been pleasantly surprised by a rare swimsuit success story. That’s why my ears perked a little when I heard the brand had <a href=\"https://fave.co/30OLa6l\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">collaborated</a> with stylist <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/rachaelwangstudio/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Rachael Wang</a>, and even more so when I read more about it: striving toward the center of that utopian Venn diagram, the collaboration struck me as an example of what fashion’s future could look like. Released in the last days of July, <a href=\"https://fave.co/30OLa6l\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">it’s a ten-piece capsule of two one-pieces and eight separates</a>, made from 100% post-consumer waste, recycled nylon and water bottles in this case—Wang has long been <a href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2019/07/sustainable-fashion-2.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a vocal advocate for bringing sustainability to the fore</a> of the conversation in fashion.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" data-instgrm-captioned Below are our thoughts on working together and how it’s brought us together—and of course some cocktail recipes for you to make at home.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong>Elizabeth:</strong> We’ve been confined to our studio apartment with our dog-baby Bow day after day since mid-March—I am no longer going into an office, and the bar Mikey bartends at closed because of the pandemic. Mikey’s never seen me in meetings with my coworkers or constituents, nor has he ever witnessed me in a “market hole” while compiling shopping for a story. I’ve never really seen him writing during the day and making cocktails at night. So here we are, seeing a side of one another we never really knew in the five and a half years we’ve been together.</p>\n<p><strong>Mikey:</strong> Liz is super focused and analytical. I’m more comfortable with winging it and taking things as they come, which is reflected in the cocktails I make during the happy hour series. I’m always aware that people may lack certain ingredients, and in my ideal world, cocktails would be way less about snobbery and more about just having delicious adult beverages. I make sure to suggest alternatives to specific ingredients throughout the videos. Our characteristics balance each other when filming, which I believe is a very important part of a relationship.</p>\n<p><strong>Elizabeth:</strong> We always had staples in our home bar—many of which we get DMs about how to use—but, as quarantine progresses, so does our bar. Pre-quarantine it was pretty small: I honestly never really drink (maybe once every few weeks), and Mikey was used to bartending at work, not at home. These days, our bar cart is packed with the spirits that Mikey is used to working with at his bar so he can make a good range of cocktails (and come up with some originals) for our videos. He’s always finding ways to suggest substitute ingredients for viewers who don’t have everything that a full stocked bar has.</p>\n<p><strong>Mikey:</strong> Speaking of working at bars, I always loathed the cocktail snobs, like the people who could tell the difference between an aged barrel versus oak aftertones. One time I took a mandatory sommelier course at a bar I worked at and a guest had the audacity to reference leather and soil as it related to the specific wine.</p>\n<p><strong>Elizabeth:</strong> We prefer to keep Happy Hour chill, and Mikey is the main source of that, because in reality, preparation for Happy Hour is actually quite intense! We start talking about what cocktails he’s going to make early in the week. When it’s time to go get materials, we go on the haul together (we love to go to the supermarket with each other). I coordinate with brands who we sometimes feature on the series, the sort of “market” work I’m used to for photoshoots. Day of, during set-up, I’m uptight and anxious and clumsy with the ingredients and materials. Mikey preps without any difficulty, and during filming, he’s his usual humorous, relaxed, and creative self.</p>\n<p>While I can’t keep track of which spirits are what or properly list the recipe to our viewers (I’ve never been able to perform!), Mikey speaks with ease as he bartends. We’ve gotten so fast now that we’ve honed in on our individual strengths, and while there are frustrations of course, I genuinely look forward to working with him. He’s so talented and I’m proud to have him be part of my workplace. Happy Hour is fun, sure—it’s Happy Hour! But it also is such a representation of our relationship, our balance as a couple.</p>\n<p><strong>Mikey:</strong> Fixing these cocktails up each week helps me recreate the social parts of the industry that I miss. Hanging out with friends and coworkers, meeting new people, letting them in on some tips and tricks I’ve learned and just paying forward the skills the great bartenders I’ve worked with taught me. And of course, hanging with Liz. At the end of the day, I hope that you guys enjoy our series and get ideas to spruce up your next Zoom happy hour or make something for a special occasion.</p>\n<p>On that note, below are three cocktails I’ve made for the segment. Cheers!</p>\n<hr />\n<h2><b>1. The Spicy Sandia </b></h2>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213602 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Drink_Recipes_-2.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! Love!\" width=\"1333\" height=\"2000\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Make your watermelon juice by blending watermelon in a blender and then straining the juice from the pulp. Fill a glass with ice cubes + frozen watermelon cubes. Add watermelon juice, lime juice, triple sec or Cointreau, Ancho Reyes and/or jalapeno slices, and tequila. Rub lime juice on the rim of your glass and add Tajín to it.</span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213595 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/the-spicy-sandia_2.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! Love!\" width=\"2100\" height=\"1133\" /></p>\n<h2><b>2. The Cucumber East River</b></h2>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213608 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Drink_Recipes_-1-2.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! Love!\" width=\"1333\" height=\"2000\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Peel the cucumber, reserving part of its peel for a ribbon garnish. Juice a cucumber or blend it in a blender and then strain the juice from the pulp. Mix the cucumber juice and sugar and warm it up over the stove or in the microwave and shake in a jar to ensure it’s mixed. Fill a Mason jar with ice. Add cucumber and sugar solution, plus lime juice, cucumber syrup, and rum or other clear spirit. Shake and top off with Champagne or club soda and a cucumber ribbon.</span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213593 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/The-Cucumber-East-River.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! Love!\" width=\"2100\" height=\"950\" /></p>\n<h2><b>3. The Matcha Cosmo Wake Up</b></h2>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213603 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Drink_Recipes_-3.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! Love!\" width=\"1333\" height=\"2000\" /></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Fill a mason jar or shaker with ice. Add lemon juice, triple sec or Cointreau, and vodka, topping off with matcha. Shake and strain through a fine mesh strainer into another glass. </span></p>\n<p><img class=\"size-full wp-image-213592 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/The-Matcha-Cosmo-Wake-Up.jpg\" alt=\"3 Cocktail Recipes Made With! 19.webp","https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/YLM-Sarai-11-600x600.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn1@2020_3/2020/08/16/10-18-29-272_ea7568ccd1865886.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","title":"Everything You’ve Ever Wanted to Know About Menstrual Cups (Including the Best One for Period Sex)","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213419","description":"<p>I remember when I first held a menstrual cup in the palm of my hand. It looked like a kitchen tool for a domesticated cat. A goblet fit for a squirrel. I couldn’t for the life of me understand how that small, snappy cup planned to enter my vaginal canal and… stay there?</p>\n<p>I remember thinking to myself:<em> I could use a comprehensive, A-to-Z guide on this tiniest of Holy Grails.</em> (Not exactly those words, but you get it.)</p>\n<p>With the state of the world being what it is—and with a personal pledge to create less waste in 2020—it feels like there’s no better time to ditch my tampons once-and-for-all for the sustainable alternative. Together with the team at <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intimina</a>, a Swedish brand offering a full range of responsibly manufactured products dedicated to menstrual care, I asked those who bleed monthly in the Man Repeller audience for all their questions and qualms about menstrual cups. And lo, did you query!</p>\n<p>Below, enjoy a guide from yours truly—made with help from the experts at <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intimina</a>, who provided some background on questions from novice menstrual cup users and menstrual cup maestros alike.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-213439 size-full\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/200807_man_repeller_intimina_0232.jpg\" alt=\"INTIMINA Ziggy Cup\" width=\"1400\" height=\"1400\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><strong>1. Finding the Mini Chalice That’s Right for You</strong></p>\n<p>The most important information for determining the right cup for you is knowing the length of your, you guessed it, cervix. Cervix height can change depending on the time of month, so <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Fblog%2Fcheck-cervix-height-menstrual-cup%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">measure it</a> with a clean finger during your cycle to be sure you know which size is right for you.</p>\n<p>Many menstrual cups come with stems! In the case of Intimina’s—apart from their <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Fziggy-cup\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">“Ziggy Cup,”</a> which you can use during sex (more on that later!!!)—you’ll be able to trim the stem to your comfort.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Fproducts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Cups can be used for up to 12 hours</a>, including during sleep, but you may need to change it more often if your flow is heavier. The good news is… there’s a cup for that. And with time, and practice, you’ll be able to determine how often you’ll need to empty your cup—anywhere from 2-3 times a day is recommended.</p>\n<p>As far as materials, medical-grade silicone cups are your best bet, since they are hypoallergenic, latex-free, and toxin-free. No microplastics, toxic chemicals, or phthalates, <em>s’il vous plaît!</em> Look for a cup that has been tested and FDA-approved for biocompatibility. Intimina happens to have a queenly starter cup—the <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Flily-cup-one\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#8220;Lily Cup One&#8221;</a>—which is, certifiably, a beginner&#8217;s best friend. It collapses down to fit into its own carrying case, and even has a removal loop to make sure your first reaction when trying it out isn&#8217;t <em>panic!</em> And if you want something even slimmer and slippier, they make a <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Flily-cup-compact\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#8220;Lily Cup <em>compact</em>&#8220;</a> which collapses all the way flat and also fits into its own precious carrying case. It&#8217;s very cute. Just saying.</p>\n<p><strong>2. Safety First, Kids</strong></p>\n<p>“What about my IUD?” many asked. I, too, am an IUD proprietor and went down the road of being confused about whether my cup would interfere with the tiny strings at the back of my canal, or that the pressure vacuum might dislodge it. Fortunately, menstrual cups are held in a lower position than a tampon and shouldn’t interfere with an internal birth control device. Experts told me that. And as far as the aforementioned pressure vacuum, if you are a new IUD user it is worth waiting a few months before incorporating a menstrual cup into your routine. If you’re concerned about the placement of your IUD, it’s worth checking in with your doctor to confirm it’s positioned correctly, that a menstrual cup won&#8217;t interfere with its placement, and that its strings aren’t too long.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-213557 size-full\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/200807_man_repeller_intimina_0444-final.jpg\" alt=\"INTIMINA Lily Cup Compact\" width=\"1600\" height=\"2000\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><strong>3. But… How Do You Clean It? Like, Really Clean It.</strong></p>\n<p>For me, this historically felt like the biggest barrier to getting a menstrual cup. Getting my hands dirty with my own period blood seemed like an <em>ick!</em> But I had to interrogate what it was about my period that made it feel like it was “dirty” or “gross,” because—pardon me, I’m mounting my soap box—it’s the most natural thing in the world and society told me it wasn’t. Women have been menstruating since time immemorial—and despite the aches and pains and occasional frustration, it is our—dare I say it, <em>beautiful</em>—biology. L’origine du monde. Whenever I get red-cheeked over my period, I just check myself and play <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MJ0QatzktZ0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">this scene</a> in my head.</p>\n<p>Okay, now: How to clean your cup! While using your menstrual cup, you can wash it in a sink with mild, PH-balanced soap and hot water. Zing. For a more thorough clean between periods, though, it’s recommended that you boil your cup submerged in a pot of water for 5 to 8 minutes. Many audience members mentioned cup staining as a pain point, and I think I may have the secret sauce! According to an expert at <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intimina</a>, mix equal parts 1% hydrogen peroxide and water in a bowl, leaving the cup submerged for 24 hours. After doing so—and before using or storing it!—be sure to wash it with warm water, to ensure that you’ve removed all the hydrogen peroxide residue. Alternatively, a 1:2 part white vinegar and water mixture will work with this method—submerge the cup in it for 24 hours and wash it thoroughly afterwards. If your cup smells like a salt &#38; vinegar chip the next day, boil it in water per the directions above.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-213440 size-full\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/200807_man_repeller_intimina_0251.jpg\" alt=\"INTIMINA Lily Cup Compact \" width=\"1600\" height=\"2000\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><strong>4. In the Words of One Responder: “How Do I Clean My Cup in a Public Restroom Without Looking Like I Murdered Someone in There???”</strong></p>\n<p>Moons ago, when I first started thinking about a menstrual cup, I imagined cleaning it out in a public bathroom stall and the resulting crime-scene vibe. A flutter of panic!!! Many responses echoed this same fear.</p>\n<p>But it doesn’t need to be scary! Wash your hands with soap and water before handling the cup, or consider carrying *coveted* hand sanitizer or antibacterial hand wipes in your bag to get clean before removing it. Chic. If you don’t have access to running water, according to the experts, it’s perfectly safe to empty your cup and wipe it out with toilet paper before reinserting. Alternatively, you can bring your reusable water bottle into the stall with you to do a little rinse. Clean your hands to the best of your ability before leaving the stall, give them a proper wash in the sink, and cartwheel out of there.</p>\n<p><strong>5. UGH, Not <em>Leakage</em></strong></p>\n<p>Leaking is not fun or cool. But just a reminder that, in the beginning, it happens! If you’re getting used to a cup, be open to the fact that leaking might be a part of the process. But if you’re still getting grief after that introductory period, the <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intimina</a> team recommends the following:</p>\n<p>There are two possible reasons for leaks: Your cup isn’t opened up properly—or it’s not positioned correctly. First and foremost, get acquainted with your ~interior architecture~ so you can visualize what you’re doing during insertion. If your cup hasn’t opened up properly, it’s all about getting the insertion method down. First, relax. No tight walls, pls. Try a different fold if the one you’re using isn’t working (<a href=\"https://youtu.be/L7DBJJhUGZE?t=36\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">here’s a handy vid for that</a>). Run a finger around the edge of the cup’s body to check for any folds. If they’re still there, gently pull or wiggle the stem. If it’s a matter of leakage due to position, experts recommend moving your cup just a little higher toward your cervix.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-213437 size-full\" src=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/200807_man_repeller_intimina_0221.jpg\" alt=\"INTIMINA Ziggy Cup\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1333\" /></p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><strong>6. Truth or Lie: You Can Have Penetrative Sex With a Cup In</strong></p>\n<p>Lest I lead you astray, it’s important to note: For most cups, it is not a good idea to have sex with it in!</p>\n<p>However, <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Intimina</a> makes a special cup specifically for penetrative sex called the <a href=\"https://click.linksynergy.com/deeplink?id=IUHkUHMX8cs&#38;mid=41390&#38;murl=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.intimina.com%2Fziggy-cup\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">“Ziggy Cup”</a>—WOOT. The first of its kind, actually. It sits high in the vaginal canal, right under the cervix, and it’s shaped more like a diaphragm than other cups. Give it a whirl and tell me what you think?</p>\n<p>So… are you convinced that now is the time to get cup’t? Will you join me on this journey to banishing tampons and liners for the sustainable alternative?? I’m fielding additional questions in the comments—and will continue consulting the experts—so drop a thought or feeling anytime.</p>\n<section class=\"Inline-shopping-block Inline-shopping 18:18:24","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","title":"6 People Who Are Making Instagram, Art, and Fashion Way More Fun","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213073","description":"<p>I’ve always loved when people have toed the line between one thing and another. Being at an intersection of two special things—or several unexpected things, even—is the stuff that makes the earth turn. To be eclectic! Multifarious. Boundless. [Insert SAT word here.]</p>\n<p>For many artists who would describe themselves as such, Instagram has become a platform for them to show off the many feathers in their hat—in some cases, literally. In the past few years I’ve specifically noticed—via Instagram, my primary platform other than TikTok—a preponderance of artists who have engaged specifically in the Venn diagram overlap of fashion, irreverence, and, of course, artistry. From egg bralettes to shoes with teeth, every time these artists&#8217; pieces slipped into my Instagram feed, my eyeballs would wobble in their sockets for a bit and I would think <em>How did they come up with something this unique???</em></p>\n<p>As a long-time fan of these creative minds, I decided it was time to be a first-time caller. Below, I ask six of the creatives occupying this special corner of the art world (and by extension, the internet) about how they landed where they did and what’s coming up next.</p>\n<hr />\n<h2>Gab Bois, Montreal, Québec</h2>\n<p><em><strong>The Cheeky Québecois Artist Making Bras Out of Tomatoes</strong></em></p>\n<p><strong>What do you consider to be your first Instagram post as an artist? </strong></p>\n<blockquote class=\"instagram-media\" data-instgrm-captioned data-instgrm-permalink=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/BMzUqXCDaeP/?utm_source=ig_embed&#38;utm_campaign=loading\" posted a photo of myself in a cream lace and tweed baker hat—it was the first post in a series of raw headshot photos of myself, family, and friends, all wearing hats I made from scrap fabrics and upcycled materials. At that time, I was freelancing as a design assistant but work was drying up, so I just made stuff I wanted to wear to stay creatively stimulated.</p>\n<p>Before posting this pic, I didn’t have much confidence in showing my ideas—I had it in my head that I should only show glossy photos of my work. I kept getting compliments on the street whenever I would wear one of my hats and was like Fuck it, no one’s never going to see my work if I’m going to be so strict in the way I should present it. font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"2020-03-06T12:54:58+00:00\">Mar 6, 2020 at 4:54am PST</time></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script></p>\n<p>At the end of last year, I made this custom giant cat-ear bonnet for a shoot inspired by anime Tekkonkinkreet. I wanted the hat to look like a black-and-white comic drawing, as if the character in a hat walked off the pages of a comic book. I used scrap wadding and upcycled a crappy women’s black faux-fur jacket. I used the black textured fur as piping and appliqued strips to mimic anime drawing outlines and details.</p>\n<p><strong>What’s one piece you’ve made that genuinely makes you laugh, or feel giant white faux-fur ball hat for designer Leeann Huang’s Central Saint Martins MA collection. Leeann wanted to achieve the look of a headpiece that was like a giant cloud. It needed to be large but light, maintain its round shape, and be comfortable to wear. When I saw the hat in context with Leeann’s collection, I was like “Wow! That’s stupidly fab!” I had never made such a huge hat before and was scared it would deflate or just fall off, but overall it was fab and fun.</p>\n<p><strong>What’s your next project?</strong></p>\n<p>I just worked on another collaboration hat for artist/designer Ed Curtis for his new collection. It’s mega stupidly fun! I just want to get back into making new hats I’d like to wear, really.</p>\n<p><strong>Who are a few artists/designers/creatives you think are doing cool stuff these days that not enough people know href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/B19tNZ4lyyR/?utm_source=ig_embed&#38;utm_campaign=loading\" style=\" color:#000; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px; text-decoration:none; word-wrap:break-word;\" target=\"_blank\">Made a new set of Bosch pants and here are some ideas behind them (link in bio 2) <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/3030.png\" alt=\"〰\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> https://www.martinacox.com/journal/bosch-pants-2018 <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/3030.png\" alt=\"〰\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> ps for those of you interested in certain ideas/inspo behind pieces and works of mine made it a personal goal this month to begin blogging once a week lil anecdotes and sources of inspo on my website, link in bio <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f98e.png\" alt=\"🦎\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /></a></p>\n<p style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px; margin-bottom:0; margin-top:8px; overflow:hidden; padding:8px 0 7px; text-align:center; text-overflow:ellipsis; white-space:nowrap;\">A post shared by <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/martinacox_/?utm_source=ig_embed&#38;utm_campaign=loading\" style=\" color:#c9c8cd; font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; font-style:normal; font-weight:normal; line-height:17px;\" target=\"_blank\"> m cox</a> (@martinacox_) on <time style=\" font-family:Arial,sans-serif; font-size:14px; line-height:17px;\" datetime=\"2019-09-03T21:28:51+00:00\">Sep 3, 2019 at 2:28pm PDT</time></p>\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"//www.instagram.com/embed.js\"></script></p>\n<p>My all-time favorite piece is my “Garden of Earthly Delights Bosch” pants; they are what pushed me to start making clothing in a fine art institution when I entered senior year at Cooper Union. I wanted to start making clothes because I had so many ideas of dream clothing items I wished existed in the real world—and this was one of them. These are also my favorite because they are a total homage to what I like to call “painstakingly slow fashion.” I really loved the idea—and humor—of spending one month on a single pair of pants. They started out as white 100% cotton I bought on 28th Street: I measured and cut the fabric into even 9 x 7-inch squares; treated each square of fabric, chose details from the painting to handprint onto every piece, patched each piece together to create the fabric, and only THEN could I begin to make the pants themselves. They took over 70 pieces of hand-painted squares to make and I loved every single one.</p>\n<p><strong>What’s one piece you’ve made that genuinely makes you laugh, or feel intensely?</strong></p>\n<p>One of my absolute favorite, hilarious, and accidental moments I experienced with a clothing item was when I first showed my “Window to the Soul” sweater in a sculpture class critique. I was wearing it with some garter belt underwear I made, and I took off my robe to wear the outfit in the center of the room while the discussion began. I was really nervous showing my work and body in this way, and being the center of attention caused my body temperature to rise—which meant that the PVC plastic window above my left breast completely fogged up. My work in a sense naturally chose to censor me as a form of protection; something I find both funny but also an incredibly interesting and performative take on how clothes can either make a wearer empowered— or vulnerable — and how interacting with a viewer or audience can dictate that or not.</p>\n<p><strong>What’s your next project?</strong></p>\n<p>Going off of the last question, I am interested in performance and clothing. I was planning for a performance in a gallery setting pre-pandemic, but that has been on the back burner since. I am definitely feeling ready to start working on some performances remotely that I want to document and I am super excited to be planning this.</p>\n<p>As for the clothing I have been making, I have taken a keen interest in repurposing vintage lingerie with <a href=\"https://shop.cafeforgot.com/shop/Martina-Cox/37\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">my clingy men</a>. I have really enjoyed toying with the materiality of vintage lingerie, specifically how in the ’50s and ’60s, the natural fibers traditionally used for loungewear/lingerie were being opted out for polyester and plastic based textiles. This idea of sleeping and being sexy “wrapped in plastic” I find really morbid but also hilarious? I think focusing on the materials that the clingy men are made out of contrast really well with these polyester based plastics in a way that really addresses their materiality.</p>\n<p><strong>Who are a few artists/designers/creatives you think are doing cool stuff these days that not enough people know about?</strong></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/hanansharifa/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hanan Sharifa</a>’s work also sells at Cafe Forgot with me. Her work delves into her Moroccan heritage and utilizes fabric in really beautiful and unique ways to address identity and the body.</p>\n<p>It was such a pleasure working with <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/fifidunks/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fiona Alison Duncan</a> (author of Exquisite Mariposa) last year for a Pillow Talk x Hard to Read events.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/346922774\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">I made a video</a> screened alongside other media contributions by Torey Thorton, Eckhaus Latta, Valentina Vaccarella just to name a few&#8230; Fashion Journalist Natasha Stagg was also there in person to read from her most recent book, Sleeveless. I just really love how Fiona enjoys<br />\nbringing fashion into these kinds of spaces and does so in really intelligent ways.</p>\n<p>Last and most importantly, my friends! Childhood friend and fellow Man Repeller writer <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/rubyredstone/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ruby Redstone</a> has been a huge source of inspo and a fashion confidant over the years. We became best friends in middle school through embarrassingly (but adorably) bonding over our love for strange haircuts, metallic spandex and just all things &#8230;.odd.</p>\n<p>Also, my best friend <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/B4Fe8QSlR0p/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sinem Gökdemir</a> is one of my favorite sources of inspo! She is my favorite person to photograph in my clothing because she has such an incredible and loving spirit that captures my clothing perfectly. I am also obsessed with her tattoos (she has a flower tattooed over her right nipple, so it was meant to be).</p>\n<h2>Nicole Mclaughlin, Brooklyn, NY</h2>\n<p><strong><em>The Artist Who Takes nostalgic for the time I spent in the village of my grandparents. Emezi","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=212272","description":"<p>The <a href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2020/07/man-repeller-book-club.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Man Repeller Book Club</a> is an experiment in connection, in relationships, in bridging the gap between internet friends and real-life, care-package-sending, yall-know-my-middle-name, how’s-your-mama-doin, kind of community. (Really, hit me in the comments, how <em>is</em> yalls mamas doin for real?) We read novels like <a href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2020/08/the-death-of-vivek-oji-akwaeke-emezi-excerpt.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Akwaeke Emezi’s <em>The Death of Vivek Oji</em></a> not only because these works of literature are brilliant and lush, but because I believe that if they are read actively, deeply, creatively, then they can teach us new ways to be in relationship with one another.</p>\n<p>On the first page of <a href=\"https://bookshop.org/a/4133/9780525541608\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the book</a>, we learn that the market burned the day Vivek, a queer boy coming of age in the political upheaval of Nigeria in the 1990s, died. This is a cold fact, a still life of a life gone to ash, a closed door. Then, on the very next page, time is winded back for us and the door swings opens: “If this story was a stack of photographs– the old kind, rounded at the corners and kept under the glass and lace doilies of center tables in parlors across the country— it would start with Vivek’s father, Chika.” This image is the invitation over the threshold and into the world of the novel.</p>\n<p>The choice to shape the doorway of the story this way does not feel like a rhetorical device so much as a setting of terms. Emezi says “The beginning image, the album and the coffee table, that&#8217;s something that to me means family history. That&#8217;s something that I grew up with. So we had that coffee table with the glass top and the family albums underneath it, and every time we went to visit another family, quite often the first thing would be, &#8220;Here, look at some albums.” We understand immediately that this is a story about and in the shape of intimate history, about kin and the blue distance between any family attempting to see and be seen by one another. We understand also that we, the readers, are visitors who can look but not own, who can stay for dinner as long as we wash our own dishes. In our conversation, Emezi and I discuss the ways that this novel tests us and asks us to come to the table, with a spicy tangent on tortured desire because you didn’t think I would be on the phone with the author of <em>Vivek’s</em> hot-ass sex scenes and <em>not</em> get a little PG-13.</p>\n<p>(This interview has been edited for clarity and to spare you most of my fawning fan girl, chaotic big crush energy.)</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nIt seems to me that this story&#8217;s relationship to the reader is more complex than a simple transmission of information. The reader can’t just walk in and receive the story—the reader has to give up some of themselves.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nYes. I definitely think that, and I think also, it’s an engagement, right? It&#8217;s an active thing. It&#8217;s not just like, &#8220;Oh, here&#8217;s the story handed to you,&#8221; and you passively take it in. I feel like it&#8217;s more active, and I feel like there are things in this book that in order for the reader to engage with them, you have to ask some questions about yourself.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nOh, yes, absolutely. Can you say more about that?</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nOne of the things is, for example, how little Vivek speaks relatively to other narratives in the book. It&#8217;s a little test, of sorts. It wasn&#8217;t designed as a test, but it does challenge the reader, I think, to ask who they are actually listening to. Are they listening to Vivek, or are they listening to everyone around Vivek and those people&#8217;s fears and those people&#8217;s perceptions of Vivek? Or are they paying attention to Vivek&#8217;s perception of himself?</p>\n<div class=\"quote none\">Are we actually listening to them, or are we listening to all the noise around them?</div>\n<p>These are two very different things, and I think it&#8217;s relevant because it affects so much of how we engage young queer people and young trans people. Are we actually listening to them, or are we listening to all the noise around them? People&#8217;s fears, people&#8217;s assumptions, and often these fears will be louder than the person&#8217;s voice, just because of the power dynamics in our society, but I want the reader to pay attention to who they&#8217;re paying attention to, because if you&#8217;re paying attention to Vivek, you come away with a completely different reading of the book than if you&#8217;re paying attention to everyone around Vivek. You come away with different ideas of what Vivek&#8217;s life is like. Different ideas around the expression and freedom.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nRight. I think that that&#8217;s one of the reasons for me that this book felt just perfect for the book club because with the book club, I want us to become aware of how the experience of reading the book transforms us. I want us to think like, “I’m making choices within my own reading of what this story means and what it means for me.” The test, then, of this book is to look through all these different eyes at Vivek and then analyze and come to an understanding of why I trusted who I trusted or believed what I believed.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nExactly.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nAnd, as you said, in many ways this mirrors the experience of queer and trans people, especially the youth. Did you consider the possibility of voyeurism in a story that is revealed primarily through the reader gazing on or at Vivek, with very little of Vivek’s own voice narrating his life? It seems like it would have been an easy trap to fall into, but I think you absolutely avoided it.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nI actually did not, but I&#8217;m really glad that I ended up avoiding it. Because, it’s like, when you&#8217;re writing a queer character who is dead from the beginning of the book, there&#8217;s a way to do it that felt right, and I feel like voyeurism would&#8217;ve been a way to do it that would&#8217;ve felt wrong.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nYeah, absolutely, and I think that’s because the looking we do in this world is a unique and active experience. Through reading this book, we’re training ourselves in a way of looking at another’s experience, and yet being consistently placed outside of the dynamic of voyeurism.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nI&#8217;m so glad to hear that. That makes my day.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nYou know, I find it really challenging to conduct this interview as an interview, because I just have so many things I want to clap for you about in this book.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nI read your book club guide on the website, and I was like, &#8220;This is the most thoughtful, tender approach to reading a book that I have ever seen in my life.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nOh my gosh—</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nI promptly sent it to a bunch of my friends. One of them texted back, and she was like, &#8220;A meditation! Time travel!” and I was like, &#8220;Yes. I know, right?&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nWell, I think the telling of this story feels so embodied, so generous with its weight! I just felt like it&#8217;s not a reciprocal reading for us to not move that same generosity into our own practice of reading the book.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nThat&#8217;s beautiful. I love that… because, look, I think a story isn&#8217;t complete until someone receives it. In order for you to be a storyteller, there has to be a story listener. Otherwise, the circle is not really complete, and I&#8217;m so appreciative of the chance to engage and talk about the work because I learn so much about the story from people who are reading it.</p>\n<p>There&#8217;s a gazillion things that I wouldn&#8217;t have thought of as I was writing that readers can discern and pull out… It becomes a thing of intersection and reflection for me as well, like your whole comment about voyeurism. I&#8217;m just like, &#8220;Oh wow.&#8221; Absolutely. Especially when it&#8217;s like a queer character living in Nigeria. I knew that when I wrote this book that there was a strong chance that people were going to read it because of that voyeurism thing of like, &#8220;Oh, let me see how terrible it is for queer people in Africa and how violent it is, and how brutal it is.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"quote none\">It was a struggle to balance the book in a way where I&#8217;m not pretending that it doesn&#8217;t suck, but at the same time, I wanted to hold space for the love and the care.</div>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nIt was a struggle to balance the book in a way where I&#8217;m not pretending that it doesn&#8217;t suck, but at the same time, I wanted to hold space for the love and the care. It sometimes surprises me when people, what they pick up from the book is like, &#8220;Oh, Vivek&#8217;s parents fear that he was going to end up as a burned and butchered body,&#8221; and I&#8217;m like, &#8220;Really? Out of everything? That was in the book? That one part was the part?&#8221;</p>\n<p>And it makes me think about the voyeurs. It makes me think of that specific gaze that wants to look at queer African people and be like, &#8220;Oh, poor you, living in a place that&#8217;s so intolerant and violent.&#8221; I didn&#8217;t want to feed that gaze.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nThese characters are rendered so tenderly that I wondered, do you fall in love with your characters?</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nI definitely do fall in love with my characters. I&#8217;m just like, &#8220;Oh, look at my little babies out there in the world. Poor buddies, having such a hard time! I really have a soft spot for Osita.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nGod, same! Poor li’l guy!</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nHe&#8217;s just having a hard time, little buddy! There&#8217;s so much tortured desire in him, which is my favorite thing in the world.</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nOh hell yeah, tortured desire. So relatable.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nSo relatable! Like why have simple desire when it can be tortured and stuff?</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nExactly.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nAnd he has so much of that in him. He has all these volatile emotions, and really this probably speaks to the folly of my dating choices in the past, that I&#8217;m just like, &#8220;Yes. Are you angry and guilty, and just not at peace with yourself? I&#8217;m into that.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nOh I totally get that, like, yes you tumultuous dark spirit! You are so troubled and I’m… kind of turned on by that?</p>\n<div class=\"quote none\">It&#8217;s kind of hot, to be quite honest, and I think that there&#8217;s this idea of tortured desire and fighting against succumbing to it</div>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nIt&#8217;s like, ugh, you&#8217;re so not okay. It&#8217;s kind of hot, to be quite honest, and I think that there&#8217;s this idea of tortured desire and fighting against succumbing to it. This idea of like, &#8220;Oh you&#8217;re resisting, you&#8217;re resisting, and then you surrender, and that moment of surrender is like a victory.” It&#8217;s just like, &#8220;Yes, you have crumbled at my feet, fantastic!” This is why I really enjoy the scenes with Osita where he does that, where he&#8217;s fighting and he&#8217;s fighting and then he breaks. I&#8217;m like, &#8220;Yes, shatter. Shatter into many glorious pieces.&#8221;</p>\n<p><strong>Sarah:</strong><br />\nI know that I absolutely shattered. I’m shattered just thinking about the steamy surrenders in this book. And, now, in a change of subject that has nothing to do with the heat gathering in my cheeks, Let’s end by talking about another “test” in the book.</p>\n<p>When we’re thinking about the fugues and the sickness that Vivek experiences. This is another opportunity to have totally different readings. Is the wasting away that he experiences part of some malady related to the sin of his queerness like some of the characters seem to believe, or from repressing his queerness by not living in his “authentic identity” as some readers might suggest, or is there another more complex, spiritual cause?</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nYeah, and I think that&#8217;s absolutely part of the test we were talking about as well—like, what is the reader bringing to this book? Because as far as I&#8217;m concerned, there&#8217;s actually no reason to assume that his sickness is because of his gender identity. So then I want the reader to ask themselves, &#8220;Why are you assuming that? Is it because queerness is pathologized in your society, and so you think, &#8216;Well, if someone is young, queer, and suffering, then they must be suffering they&#8217;re queer?'&#8221;</p>\n<p>I&#8217;m like, that&#8217;s not something that came from the book. That&#8217;s something that came from you, because if you actually look at the book and if you actually look at Vivek, like yes, he&#8217;s figuring out himself like any other teenager would be, like any other young person would be, any person in their early twenties. It&#8217;s a typical coming-of-age thing, but when I hear people say things like, &#8220;Oh, Vivek was living an inauthentic life,&#8221; who decided that? If anything, he&#8217;s expressing himself freely and he&#8217;s exploring, and I generally do not understand what&#8217;s inauthentic about that because he&#8217;s not hiding any part of himself. He looks at himself courageously.</p>\n<p><strong>Akwaeke Emezi:</strong><br />\nIf you want an example of someone who does not look at himself courageously, you could find that in Osita. He&#8217;s actually the character who is having trouble expressing himself, who&#8217;s pressing himself down, who&#8217;s suffering because of that, but no one&#8217;s flagging his suffering. I&#8217;m just like, &#8220;Why?&#8221;</p>\n<p>These are questions that have to do with the reader, not specifically with the work. That&#8217;s one of the ways in which I want the reader to reflect and think about the assumptions they&#8217;re making, and why they&#8217;re making those assumptions, and who told them those stories that led to those assumptions because the story didn&#8217;t come from this book. The story came from somewhere else.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2020/08/book-club-akwaeke-emezir-interview.html\">Every Storyteller Needs a Story Listener: Meet MR Book Club Author Akwaeke Emezi</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com\">Man Repeller</a>.</p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 12 Aug 2020 13:00:03 +0000","feedId":219,"bgimg":"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/homeauthor.jpg","linkMd5":"44de65cd3d651dbbacb6954537ae2cac","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx20/cdn22@2020_3/2020/08/16/10-18-26-626_063d7c24c3fe5cd8.webp","metaImg":"https://www.manrepeller.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/homeauthor.jpg","destWidth":896,"destHeight":896,"author":"Sarah Panlibuton Barnes"},{"createdTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","updatedTime":"2020-08-16 18:18:24","title":"12 Very Comfy, Non-Denim Shorts","link":"https://www.manrepeller.com/?p=213472","description":"<p>You&#8217;d think that the short—an abbreviated form of the pant—wouldn&#8217;t be such a tough nut to crack, and yet with every summer comes the reminder that enjoying a pair of shorts isn&#8217;t always as easy as it sounds. Denim shorts are often the barrier to entry here: once you&#8217;ve had your fair share of substandard jort experiences, it makes sense to abandon ship altogether and consider the greener pastures of summer sundresses and miniskirts.</p>\n<p>Throughout this summer, I’ve solidified a rotation of excellent casual shorts that are great to wear both at home and out and about (dogs don’t walk themselves!). These shorts are comfortable, versatile, and perfect to pair with your most casual of tees and most dressy of blouses. Check out these twelve options that make a case for being Team Short (<a href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2019/05/women-shorts.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">no matter your age!</a>), and suggestions of how to style each below.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong>1. <a href=\"https://fave.co/2CjpTrV\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"text-decoration: underline;\">The Versatile Baggie</span></a></strong></p>\n<p>If you’re well-versed in Instagram scrolling, or have frequented several of the <a href=\"https://www.manrepeller.com/2020/05/athletic-shorts-style-tips.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">previous shorts stories</a> on this very website, you will find that <a href=\"https://fave.co/2CjpTrV\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Patagonia Baggies shorts</a> are truly fan favorites. The women’s style is a bit shorter (there are two inseam options: a <a href=\"https://fave.co/3ktUfJk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">2.5 inch</a> and a <a href=\"https://fave.co/2CjpTrV\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">5 inch</a>) than the men’s (with <a href=\"https://fave.co/2XRTW1d\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">5 inch</a> and a <a href=\"https://fave.co/3fPicqS\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">7 inch</a> inseam options) — both which I wear. I think of these as the perfect alternative to a pair of denim shorts. Pair these with a crochet tank or a scarf-as-top, and you’ll have quite the “why didn’t I think of that” outfit. Comfortable and really, really cool.</p>\n<section class=\"Inline-shopping-block Inline-shopping inline-shopping-below \">\n    <div class=\"items center-lg \">\n        <a half the equation of my go-to summer outfit (athletic shorts + a summer blouse). target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"text-decoration: underline;\">The Barely-There, Yes-Frills Short</span></a></strong></p>\n<p>Okay, hear me out. Disguise</span></a></strong></p>\n<p>Pushing the envelope here, but why not try a skort? <a href=\"https://fave.co/2XQrBbO\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Outdoor Voices makes my favorite skort</a> — it has a little slit on the side that reveals its true identity. I wear mine mostly with blouses but these are also quite cool with a collegiate vintage sweatshirt or a t-shirt with a necklace or two. Add on a pair of ballet flats or glove shoes to balance out the casual.</p>\n<section class=\"Inline-shopping-block Inline-shopping inline-shopping-below \">\n    <div class=\"items center-lg \">\n
